# Praxis (Action)

In Aristotle's ethics, **praxis** (πρᾶξις) refers specifically to deliberate, rational human action. It is not merely any movement or behavior, but conduct that stems from a conscious choice ([[concepts/prohairesis]]). 

## Key Ideas

- **Distinct from Poiēsis**: Aristotle draws a sharp distinction between *praxis* (action/doing) and *poiēsis* (production/making). Making aims at an end beyond itself (e.g., building a house results in a house). Action, however, is an end in itself—acting well (*eupraxia*) is its own goal (Book VI, Chapter 2).
- **The Engine of Action**: Sense-perception originates no action (animals perceive, but do not act in this moral sense). Action is driven by the intersection of intellect and desire.
- **Sachs's Note on Praxis**: Translator Joe Sachs emphasizes that an action (*praxis*) "is chosen, and presupposes deliberation and forethought," contrasting it with the mere behavior of animals which is "guided by sensory imagination" (citing *On the Soul*, 434a 6-8).

## Primary Source Citations

### Bk. VI, ch. 2 (Bekker 1139a31-32)

```ngloss
\ex πράξεως μὲν οὖν ἀρχὴ προαίρεσις—ὅθεν ἡ κίνησις ἀλλʼ οὐχ οὗ ἕνεκα—προαιρέσεως δὲ ὄρεξις καὶ λόγος ὁ ἕνεκά τινος.
\gl πράξεως [praxeōs] [action.GEN]
    μὲν [men] [PTCL]
    οὖν [oun] [therefore]
    ἀρχὴ [archē] [origin.NOM]
    προαίρεσις— [prohairesis] [choice.NOM]
    ὅθεν [hothen] [whence]
    ἡ [hē] [the.NOM]
    κίνησις [kinēsis] [motion.NOM]
    ἀλλʼ [all'] [but]
    οὐχ [ouch] [not]
    οὗ [hou] [of-which.GEN]
    ἕνεκα— [heneka] [for-the-sake]
    προαιρέσεως [prohaireseōs] [choice.GEN]
    δὲ [de] [and]
    ὄρεξις [orexis] [desire.NOM]
    καὶ [kai] [and]
    λόγος [logos] [reasoning.NOM]
    ὁ [ho] [the.NOM]
    ἕνεκά [heneka] [for-the-sake]
    τινος. [tinos] [of-something.GEN]
\ft Now the origin of action is choice—the source of motion, but not the cause for the sake of which—and the origin of choice is desire and reasoning with a view to an end.
```

Here, Aristotle maps the exact causal chain of *praxis*. Action is not a blind reflex; its immediate origin is *prohairesis* (deliberate choice). Choice, in turn, is a compound requiring both a desire (*orexis*) for an end and the reasoning (*logos*) to achieve it. Thus, action only exists where rationality and desire intersect.

\ft For just as for a flute player and a sculptor and every craftsman, and generally for those of whom there is some product and action, the good and the well seem to be in the product, thus it would seem also for a man, if indeed there is some function of him.
```

\ex πότερον οὖν τέκτονος μὲν καὶ σκυτέως ἔστιν ἔργα τινὰ καὶ πράξεις, ἀνθρώπου δʼ οὐδέν ἐστιν, ἀλλʼ ἀργὸν πέφυκεν;

\ft Whether then are there indeed certain works and actions of a carpenter and a shoemaker, but of man there is nothing, but he is by nature idle?
```

\ex εἰ δʼ οὕτως, ἀνθρώπου δὲ τίθεμεν ἔργον ζωήν τινα, ταύτην δὲ ψυχῆς ἐνέργειαν καὶ πράξεις μετὰ λόγου, σπουδαίου δʼ ἀνδρὸς εὖ ταῦτα καὶ καλῶς, ἕκαστον δʼ εὖ κατὰ τὴν οἰκείαν ἀρετὴν ἀποτελεῖται·

\ft If thus, and we posit the function of man to be a certain life, and this to be an activity of the soul and actions with reason, and of a good man to do these things well and nobly, and each thing is completed well according to its proper virtue:

\ex νενεμημένων δὴ τῶν ἀγαθῶν τριχῇ, καὶ τῶν μὲν ἐκτὸς λεγομένων τῶν δὲ περὶ ψυχὴν καὶ σῶμα, τὰ περὶ ψυχὴν κυριώτατα λέγομεν καὶ μάλιστα ἀγαθά, τὰς δὲ πράξεις καὶ τὰς ἐνεργείας τὰς ψυχικὰς περὶ ψυχὴν τίθεμεν.
\gl νενεμημένων nenemēmenōn having been divided
    δὴ dē then
    τῶν tōn the
    ἀγαθῶν agathōn goods

    λεγομένων legomenōn being called
    τῶν tōn the ones
    δὲ de on the other
    περὶ peri concerning
    ψυχὴν psuchēn soul
    καὶ kai and
    σῶμα, sōma, body
    τὰ ta the ones
    περὶ peri concerning
    ψυχὴν psuchēn soul

    τὰς tas the

    περὶ peri concerning

    τίθεμεν. tithemen. we posit
\ft Goods having been divided then in three ways, and some being called external and others concerning soul and body, we say those concerning the soul are most authoritative and especially good, and we posit the psychic actions and activities concerning the soul.

    καλαῖς kalais noble

\ft For in addition to the things said, the one not rejoicing in noble actions is not even good:

    μὴ mē not

\ft For no one would say the one not rejoicing in doing just acts is just, nor the one not rejoicing in generous actions is generous:

    καὶ kai and
    ἐπὶ epi regarding
    τῶν tōn the
    πράξεων praxeōn actions
    μοιχεία moicheia adultery
    κλοπὴ klopē theft
    ἀνδροφονία· androphonia· murder;
\ft for some are immediately named as associated with baseness, such as spite, shamelessness, envy, and regarding actions, adultery, theft, murder;
```

\ft That moral virtue is a mean, and how, and that it is a mean of two vices, the one by excess whereas the other by deficiency, and that it is such on account of the fact that it is aiming at the mean in the passions and in the actions, has been sufficiently said.

    [ἡ] [hē] [the]
    [πρᾶξις.] [praxis.] [action.]
\ft But the involuntary being by force and through ignorance, the voluntary would seem to be of which the origin is in him knowing the particulars in which the action is.

\ex ὁ γὰρ σπουδαῖος, ᾗ σπουδαῖος, ταῖς κατʼ ἀρετὴν πράξεσι χαίρει, ταῖς δʼ ἀπὸ κακίας δυσχεραίνει, καθάπερ ὁ μουσικὸς τοῖς καλοῖς μέλεσιν ἥδεται, ἐπὶ δὲ τοῖς φαύλοις λυπεῖται.
\gl ὁ [ho] [the]
    γὰρ [gar] [for]
    σπουδαῖος, [spoudaios,] [excellent_man,]
    ᾗ [hē] [insofar_as]

    ταῖς [tais] [in_the]
    κατʼ [kat'] [according_to]
    ἀρετὴν [aretēn] [virtue]
    πράξεσι [praxesi] [actions]
    χαίρει, [chairei,] [rejoices,]
    ταῖς [tais] [in_the]
    δʼ [d'] [but]
    ἀπὸ [apo] [from]
    κακίας [kakias] [vice]
    δυσχεραίνει, [dyscherainei,] [is_displeased,]
    καθάπερ [kathaper] [just_as]
    ὁ [ho] [the]
    μουσικὸς [mousikos] [musical_man]

    ἥδεται, [hēdetai,] [is_pleased,]
    ἐπὶ [epi] [at]

    τοῖς [tois] [the]
    φαύλοις [phaulois] [bad_ones]
    λυπεῖται. [lypeitai.] [is_pained.]
\ft For the excellent man, insofar as he is excellent, rejoices in actions according to virtue, and is displeased with those from vice, just as the musical man is pleased with beautiful melodies but pained at bad ones.
```

    πράξεις, [praxeis,] [actions]
    πῶς [pōs] [how]
    πρακτέον [prakteon] [must.be.done]
    αὐτάς· [autas·] [them]
\ft Since then the present inquiry is not for the sake of theory as the others are (for we are not inquiring in order to know what virtue is, but in order to become good, since otherwise there would be no benefit from it), it is necessary to examine matters concerning actions, how they must be done.
```

    [ἀρετῆς] [aretēs] [virtue]

    [ἐπὶ] [epi] [on]
    [δὲ] [de] [on_other_hand]
    [τοῖς] [tois] [the]

    [καὶ] [kai] [and]
    [τὸ] [to] [the]

    [καὶ] [kai] [and]
    [τὰς] [tas] [the]
    [κολάσεις.] [kolaseis.] [punishments.]
\ft Since virtue is concerned with passions and actions, and on voluntary things praises and blames come to be, but on involuntary things pardon, and sometimes also pity, to distinguish the voluntary and the involuntary is perhaps necessary for those examining virtue, and also useful for lawgivers with regard to honors and punishments.

    κοινωνεῖν. [koinōnein.] [share.in.]
\ft And it is clear by the fact that animals have perception on the one hand, but do not share in action on the other.

    τʼ [t'] [and]
    ἐν [en] [in]
    ἀκμῇ [akmē] [prime]
    πρὸς [pros] [towards]
    τὰς [tas] [the]
    καλὰς [kalas] [noble]
    πράξεις· [praxeis·] [actions·]
\ft And to the young towards the faultless, and to older ones towards care and the lacking of action through weakness of help, and to those in their prime towards noble actions.
```

### Bk. 10 (Bekker 1181b20)
```ngloss
\ex ἑκάστῳ γὰρ καθʼ ἡδονήν εἰσιν αἱ οἰκεῖαι πράξεις καὶ αἱ τοιαῦται, τῶν ἀγαθῶν δὲ αἱ αὐταὶ ἢ ὅμοιαι.
\gl ἑκάστῳ [hekastō] [to_each]
    γὰρ [gar] [for]
    καθʼ [kath'] [according_to]
    ἡδονήν [hēdonēn] [pleasure]
    εἰσιν [eisin] [are]
    αἱ [hai] [the]
    οἰκεῖαι [oikeiai] [own_proper]
    πράξεις [praxeis] [actions]
    καὶ [kai] [and]
    αἱ [hai] [the]
    τοιαῦται, [toiautai,] [such_like,]
    τῶν [tōn] [of_the]
    ἀγαθῶν [agathōn] [good_men]
    δὲ [de] [but]
    αἱ [hai] [the]
    αὐταὶ [autai] [same]
    ἢ [ē] [or]
    ὅμοιαι. [homoiai.] [similar.]
\ft For to each according to pleasure are his own actions and such like, but of good men the same or similar ones.
```

### Bk. 10 (Bekker 1181b20)
```ngloss
\ex ὅπερ οὖν πολλάκις εἴρηται, οἱ περὶ τὰ πάθη καὶ τὰς πράξεις λόγοι ὁμοίως ἔχουσι τὸ ὡρισμένον τοῖς περὶ ἅ εἰσιν.
\gl ὅπερ [hoper] [which_very_thing]
    οὖν [oun] [therefore]
    πολλάκις [pollakis] [often]
    εἴρηται, [eirētai,] [has_been_said,]
    οἱ [hoi] [the]
    περὶ [peri] [about]
    τὰ [ta] [the]
    πάθη [pathē] [emotions/passions]
    καὶ [kai] [and]
    τὰς [tas] [the]
    πράξεις [praxeis] [actions]
    λόγοι [logoi] [arguments/words]
    ὁμοίως [homoiōs] [similarly]
    ἔχουσι [echousi] [have]
    τὸ [to] [the]
    ὡρισμένον [hōrismenon] [definiteness]
    τοῖς [tois] [to_the_things]
    περὶ [peri] [about]
    ἅ [ha] [which]
    εἰσιν. [eisin.] [they_are.]
\ft Which therefore often has been said, the arguments about emotions and actions similarly have their definiteness to the things about which they are.
```

### Bk. 10 (Bekker 1181b20)
```ngloss
\ex τούτοις γὰρ κοινὸν τὸ γένος καὶ αἱ περὶ τοῦτο δὴ πράξεις·
\gl τούτοις [toutois] [to_these]
    γὰρ [gar] [for]
    κοινὸν [koinon] [common]
    τὸ [to] [the]
    γένος [genos] [family/kind]
    καὶ [kai] [and]
    αἱ [hai] [the]
    περὶ [peri] [about]
    τοῦτο [touto] [this]
    δὴ [dē] [indeed]
    πράξεις· [praxeis·] [actions·]
\ft For to these the family is common and the actions about this indeed.
```

### Bk. 10 (Bekker 1181b20)
```ngloss
\ex ἅμα δὲ καὶ τῷ μὲν εὐεργέτῃ καλὸν τὸ κατὰ τὴν πρᾶξιν, ὥστε χαίρειν ἐν ᾧ τοῦτο, τῷ δὲ παθόντι οὐδὲν καλὸν ἐν τῷ δράσαντι, ἀλλʼ εἴπερ, συμφέρον·
\gl ἅμα [hama] [at_same_time]
    δὲ [de] [and/but]
    καὶ [kai] [and/also]
    τῷ [tō] [to_the]
    μὲν [men] [on_one_hand]
    εὐεργέτῃ [euergetē] [benefactor]
    καλὸν [kalon] [noble]
    τὸ [to] [the]
    κατὰ [kata] [according_to]
    τὴν [tēn] [the]
    πρᾶξιν, [praxin,] [action,]
    ὥστε [hōste] [so_that]
    χαίρειν [chairein] [to_rejoice]
    ἐν [en] [in]
    ᾧ [hō] [whom]
    τοῦτο, [touto,] [this_is,]
    τῷ [tō] [to_the]
    δὲ [de] [on_other_hand]
    παθόντι [pathonti] [one_suffering]
    οὐδὲν [ouden] [nothing]
    καλὸν [kalon] [noble]
    ἐν [en] [in]
    τῷ [tō] [the]
    δράσαντι, [drasanti,] [doer,]
    ἀλλʼ [all'] [but]
    εἴπερ, [eiper,] [if_anything,]
    συμφέρον· [sympheron·] [advantageous·]
\ft And at the same time to the benefactor the thing regarding the action is noble, so that he rejoices in him in whom this is, but to the one who suffered nothing noble is in the doer, but if anything, advantageous.
```

### Bk. 10 (Bekker 1181b20)
```ngloss
\ex τοῖς ὑπερέχουσι δὲ περὶ τὴν πρᾶξιν ἕπεται τὸ φιλεῖν καὶ τὰ φιλικά.
\gl τοῖς [tois] [to_the_ones]
    ὑπερέχουσι [hyperechousi] [excelling]
    δὲ [de] [and/but]
    περὶ [peri] [concerning]
    τὴν [tēn] [the]
    πρᾶξιν [praxin] [action]
    ἕπεται [hepetai] [follows]
    τὸ [to] [the]
    φιλεῖν [philein] [loving]
    καὶ [kai] [and]
    τὰ [ta] [the]
    φιλικά. [philika.] [friendly_things.]
\ft But to those excelling concerning the action follows loving and friendly things.
```

### Bk. 10 (Bekker 1181b20)
```ngloss
\ex τοὺς μὲν οὖν περὶ τὰς καλὰς πράξεις διαφερόντως σπουδάζοντας πάντες ἀποδέχονται καὶ ἐπαινοῦσιν·
\gl τοὺς [tous] [those]
    μὲν [men] [on_one_hand]
    οὖν [oun] [therefore]
    περὶ [peri] [about]
    τὰς [tas] [the]
    καλὰς [kalas] [noble]
    πράξεις [praxeis] [actions]
    διαφερόντως [diapherontōs] [outstandingly]
    σπουδάζοντας [spoudazontas] [being_eager]
    πάντες [pantes] [all]
    ἀποδέχονται [apodechontai] [accept]
    καὶ [kai] [and]
    ἐπαινοῦσιν· [epainousin·] [praise·]
\ft Therefore all accept and praise those being outstandingly eager about noble actions.
```
